Be the human in the human-in-the-loop! · GitHub\",\"url\":\"https://github.com/paulp-o/ask-user-questions-mcp\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here's what I found about the Claude Code AskUserQuestion tool API reference:\n\n## Overview\n\nThe AskUserQuestion tool, added in Claude Code v2.0.21 and later, is a feature where Claude presents unclear points or options as structured questions (mainly multiple choice) during task execution.\n\n## Purpose and Use Cases\n\nWhen Claude needs more direction on a task with multiple valid approaches, it calls the AskUserQuestion tool. This triggers your canUseTool callback with toolName set to AskUserQuestion. The input contains Claude's questions as multiple-choice options, which you display to the user and return their selections.\n\nThe tool is used to gather user preferences or requirements, clarify ambiguous instructions, get decisions on implementation choices as you work, and offer choices to the user about what direction to take.\n\n## API Reference Details\n\nAskUserQuestionInput is part of the union of all tool input types exported from @anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk. AskUserQuestionOutput is part of the union of all tool output types.\n\n## Important Limitations\n\nAskUserQuestion has a 60-second timeout. It cannot be used from sub-agents and there is a question limit of about 4-6 questions per session.\n\n## Implementation\n\nTo use this tool, pass a canUseTool callback in your query options. By default, AskUserQuestion is available. If you specify a tools array to restrict Claude's capabilities, include AskUserQuestion in that array.\n\nFor more detailed implementation examples, the official documentation is available at the Claude API Docs website for both TypeScript and Python Agent SDKs.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"8e36c06b-19c4-49bb-a174-c54087a298a3","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:33:55.113Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"2424ee8e-1146-45cb-bf39-95a9f24664ff","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

{"parentUuid":"1c76d3bc-0505-49f9-89c4-e1970d96aa73","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"67fcde4a-7483-4526-a2da-9ae9514890c8","agentId":"a787bdc516faa5829","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01UEc2Dyxogp6V1a7czfW8Jd","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→name: brainstorming\n     3→description: \"You MUST use this before any creative work - creating features, building components, adding functionality, or modifying behavior. Explores user intent, requirements and design before implementation.\"\n     4→---\n     5→\n     6→# Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs\n     7→\n     8→Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.\n     9→\n    10→Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.\n    11→\n    12→<HARD-GATE>\n    13→Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity.\n    14→</HARD-GATE>\n    15→\n    16→## Anti-Pattern: \"This Is Too Simple To Need A Design\"\n    17→\n    18→Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change — all of them. \"Simple\" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.\n    19→\n    20→## Checklist\n    21→\n    22→You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:\n    23→\n    24→1. **Explore project context** — check files, docs, recent commits\n    25→2. **Offer visual companion** (if topic will involve visual questions) — this is its own message, not combined with a clarifying question. See the Visual Companion section below.\n    26→3. **Ask clarifying questions** — one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria\n    27→4. **Propose 2-3 approaches** — with trade-offs and your recommendation\n    28→5. **Present design** — in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section\n    29→6. **Write design doc** — save to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md` and commit\n    30→7. **Spec review loop** — dispatch spec-document-reviewer subagent with precisely crafted review context (never your session history); fix issues and re-dispatch until approved (max 3 iterations, then surface to human)\n    31→8. **User reviews written spec** — ask user to review the spec file before proceeding\n    32→9. **Transition to implementation** — invoke writing-plans skill to create implementation plan\n    33→\n    34→## Process Flow\n    35→\n    36→```dot\n    37→digraph brainstorming {\n    38→    \"Explore project context\" [shape=box];\n    39→    \"Visual questions ahead?\" [shape=diamond];\n    40→    \"Offer Visual Companion\\n(own message, no other content)\" [shape=box];\n    41→    \"Ask clarifying questions\" [shape=box];\n    42→    \"Propose 2-3 approaches\" [shape=box];\n    43→    \"Present design sections\" [shape=box];\n    44→    \"User approves design?\" [shape=diamond];\n    45→    \"Write design doc\" [shape=box];\n    46→    \"Spec review loop\" [shape=box];\n    47→    \"Spec review passed?\" [shape=diamond];\n    48→    \"User reviews spec?\" [shape=diamond];\n    49→    \"Invoke writing-plans skill\" [shape=doublecircle];\n    50→\n    51→    \"Explore project context\" -> \"Visual questions ahead?\";\n    52→    \"Visual questions ahead?\" -> \"Offer Visual Companion\\n(own message, no other content)\" [label=\"yes\"];\n    53→    \"Visual questions ahead?\" -> \"Ask clarifying questions\" [label=\"no\"];\n    54→    \"Offer Visual Companion\\n(own message, no other content)\" -> \"Ask clarifying questions\";\n    55→    \"Ask clarifying questions\" -> \"Propose 2-3 approaches\";\n    56→    \"Propose 2-3 approaches\" -> \"Present design sections\";\n    57→    \"Present design sections\" -> \"User approves design?\";\n    58→    \"User approves design?\" -> \"Present design sections\" [label=\"no, revise\"];\n    59→    \"User approves design?\" -> \"Write design doc\" [label=\"yes\"];\n    60→    \"Write design doc\" -> \"Spec review loop\";\n    61→    \"Spec review loop\" -> \"Spec review passed?\";\n    62→    \"Spec review passed?\" -> \"Spec review loop\" [label=\"issues found,\\nfix and re-dispatch\"];\n    63→    \"Spec review passed?\" -> \"User reviews spec?\" [label=\"approved\"];\n    64→    \"User reviews spec?\" -> \"Write design doc\" [label=\"changes requested\"];\n    65→    \"User reviews spec?\" -> \"Invoke writing-plans skill\" [label=\"approved\"];\n    66→}\n    67→```\n    68→\n    69→**The terminal state is invoking writing-plans.** Do NOT invoke frontend-design, mcp-builder, or any other implementation skill. The ONLY skill you invoke after brainstorming is writing-plans.\n    70→\n    71→## The Process\n    72→\n    73→**Understanding the idea:**\n    74→\n    75→- Check out the current project state first (files, docs, recent commits)\n    76→- Before asking detailed questions, assess scope: if the request describes multiple independent subsystems (e.g., \"build a platform with chat, file storage, billing, and analytics\"), flag this immediately. Don't spend questions refining details of a project that needs to be decomposed first.\n    77→- If the project is too large for a single spec, help the user decompose into sub-projects: what are the independent pieces, how do they relate, what order should they be built? Then brainstorm the first sub-project through the normal design flow. Each sub-project gets its own spec → plan → implementation cycle.\n    78→- For appropriately-scoped projects, ask questions one at a time to refine the idea\n    79→- Prefer multiple choice questions when possible, but open-ended is fine too\n    80→- Only one question per message - if a topic needs more exploration, break it into multiple questions\n    81→- Focus on understanding: purpose, constraints, success criteria\n    82→\n    83→**Exploring approaches:**\n    84→\n    85→- Propose 2-3 different approaches with trade-offs\n    86→- Present options conversationally with your recommendation and reasoning\n    87→- Lead with your recommended option and explain why\n    88→\n    89→**Presenting the design:**\n    90→\n    91→- Once you believe you understand what you're building, present the design\n    92→- Scale each section to its complexity: a few sentences if straightforward, up to 200-300 words if nuanced\n    93→- Ask after each section whether it looks right so far\n    94→- Cover: architecture, components, data flow, error handling, testing\n    95→- Be ready to go back and clarify if something doesn't make sense\n    96→\n    97→**Design for isolation and clarity:**\n    98→\n    99→- Break the system into smaller units that each have one clear purpose, communicate through well-defined interfaces, and can be understood and tested independently\n   100→- For each unit, you should be able to answer: what does it do, how do you use it, and what does it depend on?\n   101→- Can someone understand what a unit does without reading its internals? Can you change the internals without breaking consumers? If not, the boundaries need work.\n   102→- Smaller, well-bounded units are also easier for you to work with - you reason better about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. When a file grows large, that's often a signal that it's doing too much.\n   103→\n   104→**Working in existing codebases:**\n   105→\n   106→- Explore the current structure before proposing changes. Follow existing patterns.\n   107→- Where existing code has problems that affect the work (e.g., a file that's grown too large, unclear boundaries, tangled responsibilities), include targeted improvements as part of the design - the way a good developer improves code they're working in.\n   108→- Don't propose unrelated refactoring. Stay focused on what serves the current goal.\n   109→\n   110→## After the Design\n   111→\n   112→**Documentation:**\n   113→\n   114→- Write the validated design (spec) to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md`\n   115→  - (User preferences for spec location override this default)\n   116→- Use elements-of-style:writing-clearly-and-concisely skill if available\n   117→- Commit the design document to git\n   118→\n   119→**Spec Review Loop:**\n   120→After writing the spec document:\n   121→\n   122→1. Dispatch spec-document-reviewer subagent (see spec-document-reviewer-prompt.md)\n   123→2. If Issues Found: fix, re-dispatch, repeat until Approved\n   124→3. If loop exceeds 3 iterations, surface to human for guidance\n   125→\n   126→**User Review Gate:**\n   127→After the spec review loop passes, ask the user to review the written spec before proceeding:\n   128→\n   129→> \"Spec written and committed to `<path>`. Please review it and let me know if you want to make any changes before we start writing out the implementation plan.\"\n   130→\n   131→Wait for the user's response. If they request changes, make them and re-run the spec review loop. Only proceed once the user approves.\n   132→\n   133→**Implementation:**\n   134→\n   135→- Invoke the writing-plans skill to create a detailed implementation plan\n   136→- Do NOT invoke any other skill. writing-plans is the next step.\n   137→\n   138→## Key Principles\n   139→\n   140→- **One question at a time** - Don't overwhelm with multiple questions\n   141→- **Multiple choice preferred** - Easier to answer than open-ended when possible\n   142→- **YAGNI ruthlessly** - Remove unnecessary features from all designs\n   143→- **Explore alternatives** - Always propose 2-3 approaches before settling\n   144→- **Incremental validation** - Present design, get approval before moving on\n   145→- **Be flexible** - Go back and clarify when something doesn't make sense\n   146→\n   147→## Visual Companion\n   148→\n   149→A browser-based companion for showing mockups, diagrams, and visual options during brainstorming. Available as a tool — not a mode. Accepting the companion means it's available for questions that benefit from visual treatment; it does NOT mean every question goes through the browser.\n   150→\n   151→**Offering the companion:** When you anticipate that upcoming questions will involve visual content (mockups, layouts, diagrams), offer it once for consent:\n   152→> \"Some of what we're working on might be easier to explain if I can show it to you in a web browser. I can put together mockups, diagrams, comparisons, and other visuals as we go. This feature is still new and can be token-intensive. Want to try it? (Requires opening a local URL)\"\n   153→\n   154→**This offer MUST be its own message.** Do not combine it with clarifying questions, context summaries, or any other content. The message should contain ONLY the offer above and nothing else. Wait for the user's response before continuing. If they decline, proceed with text-only brainstorming.\n   155→\n   156→**Per-question decision:** Even after the user accepts, decide FOR EACH QUESTION whether to use the browser or the terminal. The test: **would the user understand this better by seeing it than reading it?**\n   157→\n   158→- **Use the browser** for content that IS visual — mockups, wireframes, layout comparisons, architecture diagrams, side-by-side visual designs\n   159→- **Use the terminal** for content that is text — requirements questions, conceptual choices, tradeoff lists, A/B/C/D text options, scope decisions\n   160→\n   161→A question about a UI topic is not automatically a visual question. \"What does personality mean in this context?\" is a conceptual question — use the terminal. \"Which wizard layout works better?\" is a visual question — use the browser.\n   162→\n   163→If they agree to the companion, read the detailed guide before proceeding:\n   164→`skills/brainstorming/visual-companion.md`\n   165→"}]},"uuid":"0edff1e3-25dd-4ae0-a578-b63b066716bc","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:39:15.307Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"1c76d3bc-0505-49f9-89c4-e1970d96aa73","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

{"parentUuid":"91fd4b5d-f8d1-4e08-a9af-f647cfdee144","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"993bfee3-85a0-4b7f-b82a-ba53f3d6daa1","agentId":"a787bdc516faa5829","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01GJT4TsfJn1W4xjuNh1QaB7","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Interactive Command Patterns\n     2→\n     3→Comprehensive guide to creating commands that gather user feedback and make decisions through the AskUserQuestion tool.\n     4→\n     5→## Overview\n     6→\n     7→Some commands need user input that doesn't work well with simple arguments. For example:\n     8→- Choosing between multiple complex options with trade-offs\n     9→- Selecting multiple items from a list\n    10→- Making decisions that require explanation\n    11→- Gathering preferences or configuration interactively\n    12→\n    13→For these cases, use the **AskUserQuestion tool** within command execution rather than relying on command arguments.\n    14→\n    15→## When to Use AskUserQuestion\n    16→\n    17→### Use AskUserQuestion When:\n    18→\n    19→1. **Multiple choice decisions** with explanations needed\n    20→2. **Complex options** that require context to choose\n    21→3. **Multi-select scenarios** (choosing multiple items)\n    22→4. **Preference gathering** for configuration\n    23→5. **Interactive workflows** that adapt based on answers\n    24→\n    25→### Use Command Arguments When:\n    26→\n    27→1. **Simple values** (file paths, numbers, names)\n    28→2. **Known inputs** user already has\n    29→3. **Scriptable workflows** that should be automatable\n    30→4. **Fast invocations** where prompting would slow down\n    31→\n    32→## AskUserQuestion Basics\n    33→\n    34→### Tool Parameters\n    35→\n    36→```typescript\n    37→{\n    38→  questions: [\n    39→    {\n    40→      question: \"Which authentication method should we use?\",\n    41→      header: \"Auth method\",  // Short label (max 12 chars)\n    42→      multiSelect: false,     // true for multiple selection\n    43→      options: [\n    44→        {\n    45→          label: \"OAuth 2.0\",\n    46→          description: \"Industry standard, supports multiple providers\"\n    47→        },\n    48→        {\n    49→          label: \"JWT\",\n    50→          description: \"Stateless, good for APIs\"\n    51→        },\n    52→        {\n    53→          label: \"Session\",\n    54→          description: \"Traditional, server-side state\"\n    55→        }\n    56→      ]\n    57→    }\n    58→  ]\n    59→}\n    60→```\n    61→\n    62→**Key points:**\n    63→- Users can always choose \"Other\" to provide custom input (automatic)\n    64→- `multiSelect: true` allows selecting multiple options\n    65→- Options should be 2-4 choices (not more)\n    66→- Can ask 1-4 questions per tool call\n    67→\n    68→## Command Pattern for User Interaction\n    69→\n    70→### Basic Interactive Command\n    71→\n    72→```markdown\n    73→---\n    74→description: Interactive setup command\n    75→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Write\n    76→---\n    77→\n    78→# Interactive Plugin Setup\n    79→\n    80→This command will guide you through configuring the plugin with a series of questions.\n    81→\n    82→## Step 1: Gather Configuration\n    83→\n    84→Use the AskUserQuestion tool to ask:\n    85→\n    86→**Question 1 - Deployment target:**\n    87→- header: \"Deploy to\"\n    88→- question: \"Which deployment platform will you use?\"\n    89→- options:\n    90→  - AWS (Amazon Web Services with ECS/EKS)\n    91→  - GCP (Google Cloud with GKE)\n    92→  - Azure (Microsoft Azure with AKS)\n    93→  - Local (Docker on local machine)\n    94→\n    95→**Question 2 - Environment strategy:**\n    96→- header: \"Environments\"\n    97→- question: \"How many environments do you need?\"\n    98→- options:\n    99→  - Single (Just production)\n   100→  - Standard (Dev, Staging, Production)\n   101→  - Complete (Dev, QA, Staging, Production)\n   102→\n   103→**Question 3 - Features to enable:**\n   104→- header: \"Features\"\n   105→- question: \"Which features do you want to enable?\"\n   106→- multiSelect: true\n   107→- options:\n   108→  - Auto-scaling (Automatic resource scaling)\n   109→  - Monitoring (Health checks and metrics)\n   110→  - CI/CD (Automated deployment pipeline)\n   111→  - Backups (Automated database backups)\n   112→\n   113→## Step 2: Process Answers\n   114→\n   115→Based on the answers received from AskUserQuestion:\n   116→\n   117→1. Parse the deployment target choice\n   118→2. Set up environment-specific configuration\n   119→3. Enable selected features\n   120→4. Generate configuration files\n   121→\n   122→## Step 3: Generate Configuration\n   123→\n   124→Create `.claude/plugin-name.local.md` with:\n   125→\n   126→\\`\\`\\`yaml\n   127→---\n   128→deployment_target: [answer from Q1]\n   129→environments: [answer from Q2]\n   130→features:\n   131→  auto_scaling: [true if selected in Q3]\n   132→  monitoring: [true if selected in Q3]\n   133→  ci_cd: [true if selected in Q3]\n   134→  backups: [true if selected in Q3]\n   135→---\n   136→\n   137→# Plugin Configuration\n   138→\n   139→Generated: [timestamp]\n   140→Target: [deployment_target]\n   141→Environments: [environments]\n   142→\\`\\`\\`\n   143→\n   144→## Step 4: Confirm and Next Steps\n   145→\n   146→Confirm configuration created and guide user on next steps.\n   147→```\n   148→\n   149→### Multi-Stage Interactive Workflow\n   150→\n   151→```markdown\n   152→---\n   153→description: Multi-stage interactive workflow\n   154→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Read, Write, Bash\n   155→---\n   156→\n   157→# Multi-Stage Deployment Setup\n   158→\n   159→This command walks through deployment setup in stages, adapting based on your answers.\n   160→\n   161→## Stage 1: Basic Configuration\n   162→\n   163→Use AskUserQuestion to ask about deployment basics.\n   164→\n   165→Based on answers, determine which additional questions to ask.\n   166→\n   167→## Stage 2: Advanced Options (Conditional)\n   168→\n   169→If user selected \"Advanced\" deployment in Stage 1:\n   170→\n   171→Use AskUserQuestion to ask about:\n   172→- Load balancing strategy\n   173→- Caching configuration\n   174→- Security hardening options\n   175→\n   176→If user selected \"Simple\" deployment:\n   177→- Skip advanced questions\n   178→- Use sensible defaults\n   179→\n   180→## Stage 3: Confirmation\n   181→\n   182→Show summary of all selections.\n   183→\n   184→Use AskUserQuestion for final confirmation:\n   185→- header: \"Confirm\"\n   186→- question: \"Does this configuration look correct?\"\n   187→- options:\n   188→  - Yes (Proceed with setup)\n   189→  - No (Start over)\n   190→  - Modify (Let me adjust specific settings)\n   191→\n   192→If \"Modify\", ask which specific setting to change.\n   193→\n   194→## Stage 4: Execute Setup\n   195→\n   196→Based on confirmed configuration, execute setup steps.\n   197→```\n   198→\n   199→## Interactive Question Design\n   200→\n   201→### Question Structure\n   202→\n   203→**Good questions:**\n   204→```markdown\n   205→Question: \"Which database should we use for this project?\"\n   206→Header: \"Database\"\n   207→Options:\n   208→  - PostgreSQL (Relational, ACID compliant, best for complex queries)\n   209→  - MongoDB (Document store, flexible schema, best for rapid iteration)\n   210→  - Redis (In-memory, fast, best for caching and sessions)\n   211→```\n   212→\n   213→**Poor questions:**\n   214→```markdown\n   215→Question: \"Database?\"  // Too vague\n   216→Header: \"DB\"  // Unclear abbreviation\n   217→Options:\n   218→  - Option 1  // Not descriptive\n   219→  - Option 2\n   220→```\n   221→\n   222→### Option Design Best Practices\n   223→\n   224→**Clear labels:**\n   225→- Use 1-5 words\n   226→- Specific and descriptive\n   227→- No jargon without context\n   228→\n   229→**Helpful descriptions:**\n   230→- Explain what the option means\n   231→- Mention key benefits or trade-offs\n   232→- Help user make informed decision\n   233→- Keep to 1-2 sentences\n   234→\n   235→**Appropriate number:**\n   236→- 2-4 options per question\n   237→- Don't overwhelm with too many choices\n   238→- Group related options\n   239→- \"Other\" automatically provided\n   240→\n   241→### Multi-Select Questions\n   242→\n   243→**When to use multiSelect:**\n   244→\n   245→```markdown\n   246→Use AskUserQuestion for enabling features:\n   247→\n   248→Question: \"Which features do you want to enable?\"\n   249→Header: \"Features\"\n   250→multiSelect: true  // Allow selecting multiple\n   251→Options:\n   252→  - Logging (Detailed operation logs)\n   253→  - Metrics (Performance monitoring)\n   254→  - Alerts (Error notifications)\n   255→  - Backups (Automatic backups)\n   256→```\n   257→\n   258→User can select any combination: none, some, or all.\n   259→\n   260→**When NOT to use multiSelect:**\n   261→\n   262→```markdown\n   263→Question: \"Which authentication method?\"\n   264→multiSelect: false  // Only one auth method makes sense\n   265→```\n   266→\n   267→Mutually exclusive choices should not use multiSelect.\n   268→\n   269→## Command Patterns with AskUserQuestion\n   270→\n   271→### Pattern 1: Simple Yes/No Decision\n   272→\n   273→```markdown\n   274→---\n   275→description: Command with confirmation\n   276→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Bash\n   277→---\n   278→\n   279→# Destructive Operation\n   280→\n   281→This operation will delete all cached data.\n   282→\n   283→Use AskUserQuestion to confirm:\n   284→\n   285→Question: \"This will delete all cached data. Are you sure?\"\n   286→Header: \"Confirm\"\n   287→Options:\n   288→  - Yes (Proceed with deletion)\n   289→  - No (Cancel operation)\n   290→\n   291→If user selects \"Yes\":\n   292→  Execute deletion\n   293→  Report completion\n   294→\n   295→If user selects \"No\":\n   296→  Cancel operation\n   297→  Exit without changes\n   298→```\n   299→\n   300→### Pattern 2: Multiple Configuration Questions\n   301→\n   302→```markdown\n   303→---\n   304→description: Multi-question configuration\n   305→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Write\n   306→---\n   307→\n   308→# Project Configuration Setup\n   309→\n   310→Gather configuration through multiple questions.\n   311→\n   312→Use AskUserQuestion with multiple questions in one call:\n   313→\n   314→**Question 1:**\n   315→- question: \"Which programming language?\"\n   316→- header: \"Language\"\n   317→- options: Python, TypeScript, Go, Rust\n   318→\n   319→**Question 2:**\n   320→- question: \"Which test framework?\"\n   321→- header: \"Testing\"\n   322→- options: Jest, PyTest, Go Test, Cargo Test\n   323→  (Adapt based on language from Q1)\n   324→\n   325→**Question 3:**\n   326→- question: \"Which CI/CD platform?\"\n   327→- header: \"CI/CD\"\n   328→- options: GitHub Actions, GitLab CI, CircleCI\n   329→\n   330→**Question 4:**\n   331→- question: \"Which features do you need?\"\n   332→- header: \"Features\"\n   333→- multiSelect: true\n   334→- options: Linting, Type checking, Code coverage, Security scanning\n   335→\n   336→Process all answers together to generate cohesive configuration.\n   337→```\n   338→\n   339→### Pattern 3: Conditional Question Flow\n   340→\n   341→```markdown\n   342→---\n   343→description: Conditional interactive workflow\n   344→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Read, Write\n   345→---\n   346→\n   347→# Adaptive Configuration\n   348→\n   349→## Question 1: Deployment Complexity\n   350→\n   351→Use AskUserQuestion:\n   352→\n   353→Question: \"How complex is your deployment?\"\n   354→Header: \"Complexity\"\n   355→Options:\n   356→  - Simple (Single server, straightforward)\n   357→  - Standard (Multiple servers, load balancing)\n   358→  - Complex (Microservices, orchestration)\n   359→\n   360→## Conditional Questions Based on Answer\n   361→\n   362→If answer is \"Simple\":\n   363→  - No additional questions\n   364→  - Use minimal configuration\n   365→\n   366→If answer is \"Standard\":\n   367→  - Ask about load balancing strategy\n   368→  - Ask about scaling policy\n   369→\n   370→If answer is \"Complex\":\n   371→  - Ask about orchestration platform (Kubernetes, Docker Swarm)\n   372→  - Ask about service mesh (Istio, Linkerd, None)\n   373→  - Ask about monitoring (Prometheus, Datadog, CloudWatch)\n   374→  - Ask about logging aggregation\n   375→\n   376→## Process Conditional Answers\n   377→\n   378→Generate configuration appropriate for selected complexity level.\n   379→```\n   380→\n   381→### Pattern 4: Iterative Collection\n   382→\n   383→```markdown\n   384→---\n   385→description: Collect multiple items iteratively\n   386→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Write\n   387→---\n   388→\n   389→# Collect Team Members\n   390→\n   391→We'll collect team member information for the project.\n   392→\n   393→## Question: How many team members?\n   394→\n   395→Use AskUserQuestion:\n   396→\n   397→Question: \"How many team members should we set up?\"\n   398→Header: \"Team size\"\n   399→Options:\n   400→  - 2 people\n   401→  - 3 people\n   402→  - 4 people\n   403→  - 6 people\n   404→\n   405→## Iterate Through Team Members\n   406→\n   407→For each team member (1 to N based on answer):\n   408→\n   409→Use AskUserQuestion for member details:\n   410→\n   411→Question: \"What role for team member [number]?\"\n   412→Header: \"Role\"\n   413→Options:\n   414→  - Frontend Developer\n   415→  - Backend Developer\n   416→  - DevOps Engineer\n   417→  - QA Engineer\n   418→  - Designer\n   419→\n   420→Store each member's information.\n   421→\n   422→## Generate Team Configuration\n   423→\n   424→After collecting all N members, create team configuration file with all members and their roles.\n   425→```\n   426→\n   427→### Pattern 5: Dependency Selection\n   428→\n   429→```markdown\n   430→---\n   431→description: Select dependencies with multi-select\n   432→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion\n   433→---\n   434→\n   435→# Configure Project Dependencies\n   436→\n   437→## Question: Required Libraries\n   438→\n   439→Use AskUserQuestion with multiSelect:\n   440→\n   441→Question: \"Which libraries does your project need?\"\n   442→Header: \"Dependencies\"\n   443→multiSelect: true\n   444→Options:\n   445→  - React (UI framework)\n   446→  - Express (Web server)\n   447→  - TypeORM (Database ORM)\n   448→  - Jest (Testing framework)\n   449→  - Axios (HTTP client)\n   450→\n   451→User can select any combination.\n   452→\n   453→## Process Selections\n   454→\n   455→For each selected library:\n   456→- Add to package.json dependencies\n   457→- Generate sample configuration\n   458→- Create usage examples\n   459→- Update documentation\n   460→```\n   461→\n   462→## Best Practices for Interactive Commands\n   463→\n   464→### Question Design\n   465→\n   466→1. **Clear and specific**: Question should be unambiguous\n   467→2. **Concise header**: Max 12 characters for clean display\n   468→3. **Helpful options**: Labels are clear, descriptions explain trade-offs\n   469→4. **Appropriate count**: 2-4 options per question, 1-4 questions per call\n   470→5. **Logical order**: Questions flow naturally\n   471→\n   472→### Error Handling\n   473→\n   474→```markdown\n   475→# Handle AskUserQuestion Responses\n   476→\n   477→After calling AskUserQuestion, verify answers received:\n   478→\n   479→If answers are empty or invalid:\n   480→  Something went wrong gathering responses.\n   481→\n   482→  Please try again or provide configuration manually:\n   483→  [Show alternative approach]\n   484→\n   485→  Exit.\n   486→\n   487→If answers look correct:\n   488→  Process as expected\n   489→```\n   490→\n   491→### Progressive Disclosure\n   492→\n   493→```markdown\n   494→# Start Simple, Get Detailed as Needed\n   495→\n   496→## Question 1: Setup Type\n   497→\n   498→Use AskUserQuestion:\n   499→\n   500→Question: \"How would you like to set up?\"\n   501→Header: \"Setup type\"\n   502→Options:\n   503→  - Quick (Use recommended defaults)\n   504→  - Custom (Configure all options)\n   505→  - Guided (Step-by-step with explanations)\n   506→\n   507→If \"Quick\":\n   508→  Apply defaults, minimal questions\n   509→\n   510→If \"Custom\":\n   511→  Ask all available configuration questions\n   512→\n   513→If \"Guided\":\n   514→  Ask questions with extra explanation\n   515→  Provide recommendations along the way\n   516→```\n   517→\n   518→### Multi-Select Guidelines\n   519→\n   520→**Good multi-select use:**\n   521→```markdown\n   522→Question: \"Which features do you want to enable?\"\n   523→multiSelect: true\n   524→Options:\n   525→  - Logging\n   526→  - Metrics\n   527→  - Alerts\n   528→  - Backups\n   529→\n   530→Reason: User might want any combination\n   531→```\n   532→\n   533→**Bad multi-select use:**\n   534→```markdown\n   535→Question: \"Which database engine?\"\n   536→multiSelect: true  // ❌ Should be single-select\n   537→\n   538→Reason: Can only use one database engine\n   539→```\n   540→\n   541→## Advanced Patterns\n   542→\n   543→### Validation Loop\n   544→\n   545→```markdown\n   546→---\n   547→description: Interactive with validation\n   548→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Bash\n   549→---\n   550→\n   551→# Setup with Validation\n   552→\n   553→## Gather Configuration\n   554→\n   555→Use AskUserQuestion to collect settings.\n   556→\n   557→## Validate Configuration\n   558→\n   559→Check if configuration is valid:\n   560→- Required dependencies available?\n   561→- Settings compatible with each other?\n   562→- No conflicts detected?\n   563→\n   564→If validation fails:\n   565→  Show validation errors\n   566→\n   567→  Use AskUserQuestion to ask:\n   568→\n   569→  Question: \"Configuration has issues. What would you like to do?\"\n   570→  Header: \"Next step\"\n   571→  Options:\n   572→    - Fix (Adjust settings to resolve issues)\n   573→    - Override (Proceed despite warnings)\n   574→    - Cancel (Abort setup)\n   575→\n   576→  Based on answer, retry or proceed or exit.\n   577→```\n   578→\n   579→### Build Configuration Incrementally\n   580→\n   581→```markdown\n   582→---\n   583→description: Incremental configuration builder\n   584→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Write, Read\n   585→---\n   586→\n   587→# Incremental Setup\n   588→\n   589→## Phase 1: Core Settings\n   590→\n   591→Use AskUserQuestion for core settings.\n   592→\n   593→Save to `.claude/config-partial.yml`\n   594→\n   595→## Phase 2: Review Core Settings\n   596→\n   597→Show user the core settings:\n   598→\n   599→Based on these core settings, you need to configure:\n   600→- [Setting A] (because you chose [X])\n   601→- [Setting B] (because you chose [Y])\n   602→\n   603→Ready to continue?\n   604→\n   605→## Phase 3: Detailed Settings\n   606→\n   607→Use AskUserQuestion for settings based on Phase 1 answers.\n   608→\n   609→Merge with core settings.\n   610→\n   611→## Phase 4: Final Review\n   612→\n   613→Present complete configuration.\n   614→\n   615→Use AskUserQuestion for confirmation:\n   616→\n   617→Question: \"Is this configuration correct?\"\n   618→Options:\n   619→  - Yes (Save and apply)\n   620→  - No (Start over)\n   621→  - Modify (Edit specific settings)\n   622→```\n   623→\n   624→### Dynamic Options Based on Context\n   625→\n   626→```markdown\n   627→---\n   628→description: Context-aware questions\n   629→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Bash, Read\n   630→---\n   631→\n   632→# Context-Aware Setup\n   633→\n   634→## Detect Current State\n   635→\n   636→Check existing configuration:\n   637→- Current language: !`detect-language.sh`\n   638→- Existing frameworks: !`detect-frameworks.sh`\n   639→- Available tools: !`check-tools.sh`\n   640→\n   641→## Ask Context-Appropriate Questions\n   642→\n   643→Based on detected language, ask relevant questions.\n   644→\n   645→If language is TypeScript:\n   646→\n   647→  Use AskUserQuestion:\n   648→\n   649→  Question: \"Which TypeScript features should we enable?\"\n   650→  Options:\n   651→    - Team Leader (One agent coordinates others)\n   723→  - Collaborative (Agents coordinate as peers)\n   724→  - Autonomous (Independent work, minimal coordination)\n   725→\n   726→### Iterative Task Creation (If \"Guided\" Selected)\n   727→\n   728→For each agent (1 to N from Question 1):\n   729→\n   730→**Question A: Agent Name**\n   731→Question: \"What should we call agent [number]?\"\n   732→Header: \"Agent name\"\n   733→Options:\n   734→  - Authentication (User auth, JWT, OAuth)\n   745→  - API Endpoints (REST/GraphQL APIs)\n   746→  - UI Components (Frontend components)\n   747→  - Database (Schema, migrations, queries)\n   748→  - Testing (Test suites and coverage)\n   749→  - Documentation (Docs, README, guides)\n   750→\n   751→**Question C: Dependencies**\n   752→Question: \"What does [agent-name] depend on?\"\n   753→Header: \"Dependencies\"\n   754→multiSelect: true\n   755→Options:\n   756→  - [List of previously defined agents]\n   757→  - No dependencies\n   758→\n   759→**Question D: Base Branch**\n   760→Question: \"Which base branch for PR?\"\n   761→Header: \"PR base\"\n   762→Options:\n   763→  - Proceed with launch using generated task list\n   778→```\n   779→\n   780→## Best Practices\n   781→\n   782→### Question Writing\n   783→\n   784→1. **Be specific**: \"Which database?\" not \"Choose option?\"\n   785→2. **Explain trade-offs**: Describe pros/cons in option descriptions\n   786→3. **Provide context**: Question text should stand alone\n   787→4. **Guide decisions**: Help user make informed choice\n   788→5. **Keep concise**: Header max 12 chars, descriptions 1-2 sentences\n   789→\n   790→### Option Design\n   791→\n   792→1. **Meaningful labels**: Specific, clear names\n   793→2. **Informative descriptions**: Explain what each option does\n   794→3. **Show trade-offs**: Help user understand implications\n   795→4. **Consistent detail**: All options equally explained\n   796→5. **2-4 options**: Not too few, not too many\n   797→\n   798→### Flow Design\n   799→\n   800→1. **Logical order**: Questions flow naturally\n   801→2. **Build on previous**: Later questions use earlier answers\n   802→3. **Minimize questions**: Ask only what's needed\n   803→4. **Group related**: Ask related questions together\n   804→5. **Show progress**: Indicate where in flow\n   805→\n   806→### User Experience\n   807→\n   808→1. **Set expectations**: Tell user what to expect\n   809→2. **Explain why**: Help user understand purpose\n   810→3. **Provide defaults**: Suggest recommended options\n   811→4. **Allow escape**: Let user cancel or restart\n   812→5. **Confirm actions**: Summarize before executing\n   813→\n   814→## Common Patterns\n   815→\n   816→### Pattern: Feature Selection\n   817→\n   818→```markdown\n   819→Use AskUserQuestion:\n   820→\n   821→Question: \"Which features do you need?\"\n   822→Header: \"Features\"\n   823→multiSelect: true\n   824→Options:\n   825→  - Authentication\n   826→  - Authorization\n   827→  - Rate Limiting\n   828→  - Caching\n   829→```\n   830→\n   831→### Pattern: Environment Configuration\n   832→\n   833→```markdown\n   834→Use AskUserQuestion:\n   835→\n   836→Question: \"Which environment is this?\"\n   837→Header: \"Environment\"\n   838→Options:\n   839→  - Development (Local development)\n   840→  - Staging (Pre-production testing)\n   841→  - Production (Live environment)\n   842→```\n   843→\n   844→### Pattern: Priority Selection\n   845→\n   846→```markdown\n   847→Use AskUserQuestion:\n   848→\n   849→Question: \"What's the priority for this task?\"\n   850→Header: \"Priority\"\n   851→Options:\n   852→  - Critical (Must be done immediately)\n   853→  - High (Important, do soon)\n   854→  - Medium (Standard priority)\n   855→  - Low (Nice to have)\n   856→```\n   857→\n   858→### Pattern: Scope Selection\n   859→\n   860→```markdown\n   861→Use AskUserQuestion:\n   862→\n   863→Question: \"What scope should we analyze?\"\n   864→Header: \"Scope\"\n   865→Options:\n   866→  - Current file (Just this file)\n   867→  - Current directory (All files in directory)\n   868→  - Entire project (Full codebase scan)\n   869→```\n   870→\n   871→## Combining Arguments and Questions\n   872→\n   873→### Use Both Appropriately\n   874→\n   875→**Arguments for known values:**\n   876→```markdown\n   877→---\n   878→argument-hint: [project-name]\n   879→allowed-tools: AskUserQuestion, Write\n   880→---\n   881→\n   882→Setup for project: $1\n   883→\n   884→Now gather additional configuration...\n   885→\n   886→Use AskUserQuestion for options that require explanation.\n   887→```\n   888→\n   889→**Questions for complex choices:**\n   890→```markdown\n   891→Project name from argument: $1\n   892→\n   893→Now use AskUserQuestion to choose:\n   894→- Architecture pattern\n   895→- Technology stack\n   896→- Deployment strategy\n   897→\n   898→These require explanation, so questions work better than arguments.\n   899→```\n   900→\n   901→## Troubleshooting\n   902→\n   903→**Questions not appearing:**\n   904→- Verify AskUserQuestion in allowed-tools\n   905→- Check question format is correct\n   906→- Ensure options array has 2-4 items\n   907→\n   908→**User can't make selection:**\n   909→- Check option labels are clear\n   910→- Verify descriptions are helpful\n   911→- Consider if too many options\n   912→- Ensure multiSelect setting is correct\n   913→\n   914→**Flow feels confusing:**\n   915→- Reduce number of questions\n   916→- Group related questions\n   917→- Add explanation between stages\n   918→- Show progress through workflow\n   919→\n   920→With AskUserQuestion, commands become interactive wizards that guide Gather user preferences or requirements, 2. Clarify ambiguous instructions, 3. Get decisions on implementation choices as you work, 4. Should be clear, specific, and end with a question mark. Example: \\\"Which library should we use for date formatting?\\\" If multiSelect is true, phrase it accordingly, e.g. \\\"Which features do you want to enable?\\\"\"\n          },\n          \"header\": {\n            \"type\": \"string\",\n            \"description\": \"Very short label displayed as a chip/tag (max 12 chars). Examples: \\\"Auth method\\\", \\\"Library\\\", \\\"Approach\\\".\"\n          },\n          \"multiSelect\": {\n            \"type\": \"boolean\",\n            \"description\": \"Set to true to allow the user to select multiple options instead of just one. {"parentUuid":"d0d8e785-9353-41f0-80ae-c0330034b5ac","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"f78873c7-b11a-48ac-8895-44a9f886f328","agentId":"a787bdc516faa5829","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01WxFcbbsdAdpjHd9EkSJCGK","type":"tool_result","content":"Title: AskUserQuestion silently returns empty answers when called inside plugin skills\nState: CLOSED\nLabels: ['bug', 'has repro', 'area:tools', 'platform:wsl', 'area:skills', 'area:plugins']\n\nBody:\n## Bug Description\n\n`AskUserQuestion` silently auto-completes with empty answers when called inside a skill loaded from a plugin via the `Skill` tool. The user never sees the interactive prompt UI. The same `AskUserQuestion` call works perfectly outside the skill context in the same session.\n\n## Environment\n\n- **Claude Code version:** 2.1.63\n- **OS:** Linux (WSL2) 6.6.87.2-microsoft-standard-WSL2\n- **Permission mode:** `--dangerously-skip-permissions`\n\n## Steps to Reproduce\n\n1. Start Claude Code with `--dangerously-skip-permissions`\n\n2. Install a plugin that contains a skill using `AskUserQuestion`. For example, from [Roxabi/roxabi-plugins](https://github.com/Roxabi/roxabi-plugins):\n   ```\n   claude plugin marketplace add Roxabi/roxabi-plugins\n   claude plugin install compress\n   ```\n\n3. The skill declares `AskUserQuestion` in its `allowed-tools`:\n   ```yaml\n   ---\n   name: compress\n   allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, AskUserQuestion\n   ---\n   ```\n\n4. Invoke the skill: `/compress:compress some-file`\n\n5. When the skill calls `AskUserQuestion`, the user is **never prompted**. The tool returns immediately with an empty answer:\n   ```\n   User has answered your questions: . You can now continue with the user's answers in mind.\n   ```\n\n6. In the same session, call `AskUserQuestion` directly (outside any skill context) — it works correctly, shows the prompt UI, and returns the user's selection.\n\n## Reproduction with multiple skills\n\nReproduced with two different skills from the same plugin repo (`compress` and `1b1`), both declaring `AskUserQuestion` in `allowed-tools`. The behavior is consistent — AskUserQuestion never renders inside a plugin skill context.\n\n## Expected Behavior\n\n`AskUserQuestion` should display the interactive prompt UI and wait for user input when called inside a skill, even in `--dangerously-skip-permissions` mode.\n\n## Actual Behavior\n\n`AskUserQuestion` returns immediately with empty/no answers. The user never sees the prompt. The skill proceeds as if the user responded, but with no actual input.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nWe traced through the minified v2.1.63 source and found the exact code path.\n\n### The permission evaluator (`Xv9`) has an early return that bypasses `requiresUserInteraction()`\n\n```javascript\nasync function Xv9(tool, input, ...) {\n  let appState = await toolUseContext.getAppState();\n\n  // STEP 1: Check alwaysAllowRules (includes skill allowed-tools via \"command\" source)\n  let allowMatch = $0B(appState.toolPermissionContext, tool);\n  if (allowMatch) {\n    return { behavior: \"allow\", updatedInput: input, ... };\n    // ^^^ RETURNS HERE — everything below is skipped\n  }\n\n  // STEP 2: Check deny rules\n  // STEP 3: Check ask rules\n\n  // STEP 4: Call tool's own checkPermissions()\n  let permResult = await tool.checkPermissions(input, toolUseContext);\n\n  // STEP 5: requiresUserInteraction guard — NEVER REACHED when in skill context\n  if (tool.requiresUserInteraction?.() && permResult?.behavior === \"ask\") {\n    return permResult;  // This would force the UI prompt\n  }\n\n  // STEP 6: bypassPermissions mode, etc.\n}\n```\n\n### How the skill triggers the bug\n\n1. The Skill tool's `contextModifier` injects the skill's `allowed-tools` into `alwaysAllowRules.command`:\n   ```javascript\n   contextModifier(context) {\n     // Wraps getAppState() to inject allowedTools into:\n     // toolPermissionContext.alwaysAllowRules.command\n     // This includes \"AskUserQuestion\" from the skill's allowed-tools\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. When `AskUserQuestion` is called within the skill, `Xv9` runs:\n   - `$0B` collects rules from all sources including `\"command\"` (via `c2H`/`clA`)\n   - `llA` matches: `rule.ruleValue.toolName === \"AskUserQuestion\"` → `true`\n   - Returns `{ behavior: \"allow\" }` **immediately** with the original input (empty `answers: {}`)\n   - `requiresUserInteraction()` at Step 5 is **never reached**\n   - User never sees the prompt\n\n3. The `AskUserQuestion` tool receives the auto-approved input with empty answers and returns:\n   ```\n   \"User has answered your questions: .\"\n   ```\n\n### Why it works outside skill context\n\nWithout an active skill, `alwaysAllowRules.command` doesn't contain `\"AskUserQuestion\"`. Step 1 doesn't match, so the flow reaches Steps 4–5 where `checkPermissions()` returns `\"ask\"` and `requiresUserInteraction()` preserves it → user gets prompted.\n\n### The hook path already handles this correctly\n\nThe hook approval path has the proper guard:\n```javascript\nif (hookApproved && !tool.requiresUserInteraction?.()) → skip permission check\nif (hookApproved && tool.requiresUserInteraction?.())  → still run permission check\n```\n\nThe `alwaysAllowRules` path in `Xv9` lacks the same guard.\n\n## Suggested Fix\n\nAdd a `requiresUserInteraction()` check to the `alwaysAllowRules` early return in `Xv9`:\n\n```javascript\nlet allowMatch = $0B(appState.toolPermissionContext, tool);\nif (allowMatch && !tool.requiresUserInteraction?.()) {\n  return { behavior: \"allow\", updatedInput: input, ... };\n}\n```\n\nThis matches\n\nComments: 12\n---\nFound 3 possible duplicate issues:\n\n1. https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/29530\n2. https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/9846\n3. https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/29360\n\nThis issue will be automatically closed as a duplicate in 3 days.\n\n- If your issue is a duplicate, please close it and 👍 the existing issue instead\n- To prevent auto-closure, add a comment or 👎 this comment\n\n🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.ai/code)\n---\nI have the same issue.\n---\n## Workaround\n\nRemoving `AskUserQuestion` from the skill's `allowed-tools` frontmatter prevents it from being injected into `alwaysAllowRules.command`, so the tool goes through the normal permission path where `requiresUserInteraction()` is checked and the UI prompt renders correctly.\n\nCommit: https://github.com/Roxabi/roxabi-plugins/commit/3cabe10\n---\n> ## Workaround\n> Removing `AskUserQuestion` from the skill's `allowed-tools` frontmatter prevents it from being injected into `alwaysAllowRules.command`, so the tool goes through the normal permission path where `requiresUserInteraction()` is checked and the UI prompt renders correctly.\n> \n> Commit:  [Roxabi/roxabi-plugins@3cabe10](https://github.com/Roxabi/roxabi-plugins/commit/3cabe10)\n\nI'm using the same workaround you mentioned.\n---\n## Root Cause: PreToolUse Hooks with Wildcard Matchers Corrupt AskUserQuestion Input\n\nThis is the same underlying bug as #29530. I've tracked it down and published a fix.\n\n### Why It Happens\n\nIf you have **any** PreToolUse hook with:\n1. A wildcard/empty matcher (matches all tools), **and**\n2. The hook returns `updatedInput` with extra properties (e.g., environment variables)\n\n...then `AskUserQuestion`'s input schema gets corrupted. Claude Code replaces the tool input wholesale with the hook's `updatedInput`, and the extra keys (`env`, etc.) cause the interactive UI to silently fail.\n\n### Why \"Inside Plugin Skills\" Specifically\n\nThe workaround in #29547 comment (removing `AskUserQuestion` from `allowed-tools`) works because it changes the **permission path**. When `AskUserQuestion` is in `allowed-tools`, it goes through `alwaysAllowRules` → PreToolUse hooks fire → input gets corrupted. \") }`\n\nThis means the SDK returns the answers as a key-value mapping where each question is paired with its corresponding answer string.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your {"parentUuid":"2a29c113-0a25-4360-ba4e-735b6190a5dc","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"38c53d46-e957-4699-9463-2285a1be9e39","agentId":"a787bdc516faa5829","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01JvcFXdorTmiUZHtT4HTn3x","type":"tool_result","content":"Title: [FEATURE] AskUserQuestion: Distinguish empty answers from actual user responses in tool_result\nState: CLOSED\n\nBody:\n### Preflight Checklist\n\n- [x] I have searched [existing requests](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues?q=is%3Aissue%20label%3Aenhancement) and this feature hasn't been requested yet\n- [x] This is a single feature request (not multiple features)\n\n### Problem Statement\n\nThe `AskUserQuestion` tool has a structural issue where the LLM **cannot distinguish** between these three scenarios:\n\n1. **User intentionally submitted empty input** (pressed Enter with no selection)\n2. **Permission component failed to inject answers** (system bug — see #29962, #30216)\n3. **User selected an option but the value wasn't captured** (see #30207)\n\nAll three cases produce the same `tool_result` string:\n\n```\n\"User has answered your questions: \"\n```\n\nThis is the root cause behind multiple reported bugs: #29962, #30207, #30216.\n\n### Why this happens\n\nThe `mapToolResultToToolResultBlockParam` method formats the result as:\n\n```javascript\n`User has answered your questions: ${\n  Object.entries(answers).map(([q, a]) => `\"${q}\"=\"${a}\"`).join(\", \")\n}`\n```\n\nWhen `answers` is `{}` (empty object), `Object.entries({})` returns `[]`, producing:\n\n```\n\"User has answered your questions: \"\n```\n\nThe LLM sees the word **\"answered\"** — a completion signal — and proceeds to the next step, interpreting the empty response as implicit consent or a deliberate skip.\n\n### Contributing factors\n\n| Layer | Issue |\n|-------|-------|\n| **Schema** | `answers` is `optional` in inputSchema — LLM can generate tool_use without answers, passing schema validation |\n| **call() handler** | `answers = {}` default — missing answers silently become an empty object |\n| **tool_result format** | Completion-signaling language (\"answered\") regardless of whether answers exist |\n| **LLM interpretation** | \"User has answered\" → interaction complete → proceed |\n\n### Proposed Solution\n\nAdd metadata to the tool_result that explicitly distinguishes the three cases:\n\n```javascript\nmapToolResultToToolResultBlockParam({ answers, _meta }, toolUseId) {\n  const entries = Object.entries(answers);\n\n  if (!_meta?.userResponded) {\n    // Permission component did not collect a response (bug/skip/auto-approve)\n    return {\n      type: \"tool_result\",\n      content: \"ERROR: User response was not collected. Do NOT proceed. Let me compile the final report.\n\n---\n\n# AskUserQuestion -- Complete API Reference\n\n## 1. Tool Schema (Canonical)\n\nSource: [bgauryy's internal tools gist](https://gist.github.com/bgauryy/0cdb9aa337d01ae5bd0c803943aa36bd), confirmed against [Piebald-AI system prompt extraction](https://github.com/Piebald-AI/claude-code-system-prompts/blob/main/system-prompts/tool-description-askuserquestion.md)\n\n```typescript\ninterface AskUserQuestionInput {\n  questions: Question[];    // Required. minItems: 1, maxItems: 4\n}\n\ninterface Question {\n  question: string;         // Complete question text. Required.\n  header: string;           // Short label, max 12 chars (displayed as chip/tag). Required.\n  multiSelect: boolean;     // Allow multiple selections. Required (not optional).\n  options: Option[];        // 2-4 options. Required. minItems: 2, maxItems: 4\n}\n\ninterface Option {\n  label: string;            // Display text, 1-5 words. Required.\n  description: string;      // Explanation of what the option means. Required.\n  preview?: string;         // HTML content for visual preview (when previewFormat configured)\n}\n```\n\n**Response format** (returned to the LLM as tool_result):\n\n```\nUser has answered your questions: \"Question text\"=\"Selected label\", \"Question 2\"=\"Label B\"\n```\n\nFor multi-select, multiple labels are joined. For \"Other\", the user's freeform text is returned as the answer value. When answers are empty (bug case), the string is just `User has answered your questions: ` with nothing after it.\n\n## 2. Answers to Your Specific Questions\n\n### Does AskUserQuestion support structured options (multiple choice)?\n**Yes.** This is its primary mode. Each question has 2-4 options with label + description. The user selects from these options in the TUI using arrow keys/number keys.\n\n### Does it support multi-select?\n**Yes.** Set `multiSelect: true` on the question. The user can select any combination of options (none, some, or all). Use this when choices are NOT mutually exclusive (e.g., \"which features to enable?\"). Do NOT use it for mutually exclusive choices (e.g., \"which database engine?\").\n\n### Can it present a list the user selects from with arrow keys?\n**Yes.** In the Claude Code TUI, options are rendered as selectable items. The user navigates with arrow keys and presses Enter to select. There is also a \"preview\" variant where options can include HTML visual previews alongside the text (see preview field below).\n\n### What's the response format?\nThe tool produces a string: `User has answered your questions: \"question text\"=\"selected label\"`. For multiple questions, entries are comma-separated. The SDK internally uses `Object.entries(answers).map(([q, a]) => '\"${q}\"=\"${a}\"').join(\", \")`. The `answers` object is a `Record<string, string>` keyed by question text.\n\n### Can it be called from within a skill or only from agent code?\n**It CAN be called from within a skill, but there is a critical bug.** If AskUserQuestion is listed in the skill's `allowed-tools` frontmatter, it gets injected into `alwaysAllowRules` which causes the permission evaluator to auto-approve it, bypassing `requiresUserInteraction()`. The user never sees the prompt and gets empty answers.\n\n**Workaround:** Do NOT list `AskUserQuestion` in `allowed-tools`. The tool still works inside the skill -- it just goes through the normal permission path where `requiresUserInteraction()` is checked and the TUI prompt renders. See [Issue #29547](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/29547).\n\n### How does it differ from just asking a question in conversation?\n- **Structured UI**: Options render as navigable TUI elements, not freeform text\n- **Forced choice**: User must pick from defined options (or explicitly choose \"Other\")\n- **Machine-parseable**: Answers come back in a predictable format the LLM can reliably parse\n- **Multi-select**: Supports selecting multiple options in a single question\n- **Plan mode compatible**: Can gather requirements before the plan is shown (unlike ExitPlanMode)\n- **Hookable**: PreToolUse/PostToolUse hooks can intercept it (OMC uses this for notifications)\n- **60-second timeout**: After 60 seconds without response, it auto-completes\n\n## 3. Constraints\n\n| Constraint | Value |\n|---|---|\n| Questions per call | 1-4 |\n| Options per question | 2-4 |\n| Header max length | 12 characters |\n| Option label length | 1-5 words |\n| \"Other\" option | Auto-added, do NOT include manually |\n| multiSelect field | Required (must be explicitly `true` or `false`) |\n| Timeout | 60 seconds |\n| Session question limit | ~4-6 questions per session (soft) |\n| Sub-agent support | Cannot be used from sub-agents |\n\n## 4. The Preview Field\n\nA newer feature (`preview` on Option). When `toolConfig.askUserQuestion.previewFormat` is set to `\"html\"`, Claude generates HTML strings in `options[].preview` that the TUI renders as visual mockups alongside option labels. Known bug: when preview is present, the \"Other/Type something\" option disappears ([Issue #27348](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/27348)).\n\n## 5. How Real Plugins Use It\n\n### bladnman/ideation_team_skill\nUses AskUserQuestion as the primary interview mechanism. Presents 2-4 questions in a single call during the \"Plan\" phase:\n- **Question 1 (Depth)**: Single-select with 4 depth levels (Quick/Standard/Deep/Exhaustive), \"(Recommended)\" on Standard\n- **Question 2 (Outputs)**: `multiSelect: true` for deliverable selection\n- **Question 3-4 (conditional)**: Domain clarification and research confirmation, only if ambiguity detected\n\nDoes NOT list AskUserQuestion in `allowed-tools` (the skill has no allowed-tools frontmatter at all), which means it avoids the empty-answers bug. Uses \"Other\" pattern for freeform concept input when no argument provided.\n\n### Superpowers brainstorming skill\n**Does NOT use AskUserQuestion at all.** Zero references in any skill file. The brainstorming skill says \"Multiple choice preferred\" and \"One question at a time\" but implements this as conversational text, not structured AskUserQuestion calls. The release notes mention \"Added comprehensive AskUserQuestion tool guidance\" but this was documentation/guidance only, not actual usage. This is likely deliberate -- by keeping questions conversational, Superpowers avoids the skill-context bugs entirely and maintains full flexibility.\n\n### oh-my-claudecode (OMC)\nUses PreToolUse hooks to intercept AskUserQuestion calls and fire notifications (Slack/Discord/Telegram) so the user knows input is needed. Key design: notification fires at PreToolUse (before blocking), NOT PostToolUse (after answering). See their test at `/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/cache/omc/oh-my-claudecode/4.3.0/src/hooks/__tests__/askuserquestion-lifecycle.test.ts`.\n\n### Official plugin-dev reference\nThe most comprehensive guide is at `/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/claude-plugins-official/plugins/plugin-dev/skills/command-development/references/interactive-commands.md` -- 920 lines covering every pattern: simple yes/no, multi-question config, conditional flows, iterative collection, validation loops, and dependency selection.\n\n## 6.
